  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_a9b40c8a-d422-479a-b758-a4fa204736e7'
      });
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer9339066962797449351"><div><b>The millions-selling fantasy epic of the new Russian literary icon-a freeloading freebooter who finds a new home in a magical world</b><br/><br/> Max Frei's novels have been a literary sensation in Russia since their debut in 1996, and have swept the fantasy world over. Presented here in English for the first time, <i>The Stranger</i> will strike a chord with readers of all stripes. Part fanta</div></span>
  <span id="freeText9339066962797449351" style="display:none"><div><b>The millions-selling fantasy epic of the new Russian literary icon-a freeloading freebooter who finds a new home in a magical world</b><br /><br /> Max Frei's novels have been a literary sensation in Russia since their debut in 1996, and have swept the fantasy world over. Presented here in English for the first time, <i>The Stranger</i> will strike a chord with readers of all stripes. Part fantasy, part horror, part philosophy, part dark comedy, the writing is united by a sharp wit and a web of clues that will open up the imagination of every reader.<br /><br /> Max Frei was a twenty-something loser-a big sleeper (that is, during the day; at night he can't sleep a wink), a hardened smoker, and an uncomplicated glutton and loafer. But then he got lucky. He contacts a parallel world in his dreams, where magic is a daily practice. Once a social outcast, he's now known in his new world as the "unequalled Sir Max." He's a member of the Department of Absolute Order, formed by a species of enchanted secret agents; his job is to solve cases more extravagant and unreal than one could imagine-a journey that will take Max down the winding paths of this strange and unhinged universe.<br /><br /></div></span>
  <a data-text-id="9339066962797449351" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="bookReviews">
  




  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_2188050659" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2188050659" />
    <a title="Evgeny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny"><img alt="Evgeny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544797852p2/9340136.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2188050659?book_show_action=true">Nov 30, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Evgeny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Evgeny" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny">Evgeny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9340136-evgeny?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2188050659" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13380974567550269417"><b>DNF at 19%</b><br/><br/>Max Frei was a typical good-for-nothing loser; his achievement was being good absolutely for nothing. Suddenly he ended up in a magical land and it turns out he is the most useful guy around: everything he did was great, everybody loved him, and his boss made him compliments non-stop. He was working in Department of Absolute Order - secret service of the said magic land; James Bond and Sherlock Holmes put together had nothing on him. <br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1512092160i/24573227._SX540_.jpg' alt='Secret Service' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>The book consists of several interconnected novellas</span>
  <span id="freeText13380974567550269417" style="display:none"><b>DNF at 19%</b><br><br>Max Frei was a typical good-for-nothing loser; his achievement was being good absolutely for nothing. Suddenly he ended up in a magical land and it turns out he is the most useful guy around: everything he did was great, everybody loved him, and his boss made him compliments non-stop. He was working in Department of Absolute Order - secret service of the said magic land; James Bond and Sherlock Holmes put together had nothing on him. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1512092160i/24573227._SX540_.jpg" alt="Secret Service" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>The book consists of several interconnected novellas each dealing with Max untangling yet another magical mystery. <br><br>Sounds great so far? After all every single one of my friends who read it rated it with minimum 4 stars. Not so for me as I stoically read first 100 pages and stopped. One evening as I was riding home from work I read some more and stopped for good. I am breaking my own rule because of this book though. Before it DNF was equal to 1 star, period. This one however deserves more, but there is no way in Hell I am going to suffer through 600+ pages (yes, this is its length) just to be able to give it 2 stars; it is easier to bend my own rules a little. To my friends that loved it: sorry I could not do it; I hope we will remain friends. <br><br>So what did not work? I could not care less about any single character; they all looked quite flat to me at the point where I stopped. Max is worth a special discussion. The older and more cynical I become the more I believe that a professional loafer will remain true to his/her profession until the visit from the Grim Reaper. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1512092259i/24573231._SX540_.jpg" alt="Loafer" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I cannot believe that a guy in an alien world would be better suited to it than natives. Dorothy in the land of Oz was more believable - and this is a book for young kids!<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1512092335i/24573235._SX540_.jpg" alt="Dorothy" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>There was something else that did not work for me: something I cannot even point my finger to. I take an easy way out and will say that the book just did not click for me. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1512092499i/24573250._SX540_.jpg" alt="Click" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I hope all readers know what I am talking about. <br><br>In the end if you are looking to read mystery novellas set in a magic land that are effortlessly solved by a Mary Sue guy, look no further. Otherwise you might want to avoid this book (or borrow it from a library/friend to try). I really cannot see how it became "millions-selling fantasy epic of the new Russian literary icon" - this is a quote from the book blurb at the time when these lucky Russians have Strugatsky brothers, Kir Bulychev, Vladislav Krapivin, and Alexander Kazantsev - not to mention earlier classics of scifi like Ivan Antonovich Efremov and Alexander Romanovich Belyaev. 2 stars. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1512092659i/24573254._SX540_.jpg" alt="The Mystery of the Third Planet" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="13380974567550269417" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText11442718898815539448" style="display:none">-I have read it in Russian first. And was really looking forward to read it english. When I did I was very disappointed, since book heavily relies on dialogs and funny moments related to the differences of idioms in Echo in comparison to then Max is used to, a creative translation was absolutely crucial and it was not done so the final product is bellow 0 for me. Moreover after translation book turned so impersonal it is almost impossible to connect to the main character, this probably due to the fact that the personality of Max was in original book conveyed by his use of language and in translated version this peculiarities were eliminated. <br />-two examples of what I think is a bad translation<br />a)"vampire under your blanket "-firstly it is not a vampire but a [vurdolag:], which is a generic term for monster(although archaically it meant a vampire), secondly it is based on Russian"devil under your blanket", which is a mild form of curse, but since nobody in Echo knows WHAT is devil Max have to use a word monster. Perhaps if an english curse with word devil would have been used in a similar fashion it would have made much more sense<br /><br />b)In a translated version Max shouts "liquidated" to Lonli-Lokli, in response to which Shurf produces streams of water, explaining himself by saying that he have thought that the order was to "liquify" .It is not convincing, considering that the character of Lonli-Lokli, usually makes no mistakes.In russian " "water up"or"liquify", is a slang term meaning to kill and of-course Surf is unfamiliar, with russian slang, so his reaction is only natural .In my opinion if something like "cook him" from Max, followed by Lonli-Lokli pouring vegetables and spices on the head of dead magician, would make more sense and stay true to the spirit of original writing <br /><br />there are a lot more<br /></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/435274547?book_show_action=true">Oct 16, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ieva Gurklyte" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ieva Gurklyte" href="/user/show/13680547-ieva-gurklyte">Ieva Gurklyte</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer435274547" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2946277899573716365">I have read this book like 10 times now! I love Echo, all the characters, their funny conversations and magic without logic and explanations. The thing is, I read the series as much as they are published in Lithuanian and I found the translation really good. Maybe it is because it is Eastern Europe and kind of similar cultural background (like all the jokes, irony and etc., oh, and the author is living Vilnius, Lithuania). I found English translation a bit disappointing but unless you speak Russ</span>
  <span id="freeText2946277899573716365" style="display:none">I have read this book like 10 times now! I love Echo, all the characters, their funny conversations and magic without logic and explanations. The thing is, I read the series as much as they are published in Lithuanian and I found the translation really good. Maybe it is because it is Eastern Europe and kind of similar cultural background (like all the jokes, irony and etc., oh, and the author is living Vilnius, Lithuania). I found English translation a bit disappointing but unless you speak Russian there is not much choice. I guess this sort of fantasy is not for everyone. Magic is not explained, we do not really know much background of Max's previous life and all the descriptions of Echo and the lifestyle there are not detailed. You have to use imagination and I love it! I adore those strange, unfamiliar names, places, habits (like taking 8 baths and wearing turbans and stuff), bedroom floor as a mattress, and how Max has this crazy luck to get out of all the messed up situations with so little effort. Every single time I turn a random page and read I laugh every five minutes. It is not the suspense and action that drives this novel but the amazing setting, characters and vivid language.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2946277899573716365" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_413829089" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/413829089" />
    <a title="Valeria" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12808806-valeria"><img alt="Valeria" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1347580687p2/12808806.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/413829089?book_show_action=true">Sep 13, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Valeria" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Valeria" href="/user/show/12808806-valeria">Valeria</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer413829089" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3889704710532561143">I read this book in Russian in 2000, when it was published under the name of "The Labyrinth". I've read it about 15 times since then. Now I'm enjoying every second of reading the translated version of it.<br/>Once you get accustomed to the writer's quaint manner of writing you will love it too. The first thing that meets the eye is the unique style of narration and the unusual choice of words. It's not casual, but not as pompous and epic as traditional fantasy. It's rather self-ironic and even sarcas</span>
  <span id="freeText3889704710532561143" style="display:none">I read this book in Russian in 2000, when it was published under the name of "The Labyrinth". I've read it about 15 times since then. Now I'm enjoying every second of reading the translated version of it.<br />Once you get accustomed to the writer's quaint manner of writing you will love it too. The first thing that meets the eye is the unique style of narration and the unusual choice of words. It's not casual, but not as pompous and epic as traditional fantasy. It's rather self-ironic and even sarcastic at times.<br /><br />When I read this book in original language, as a keen linguist, I wondered if this book will ever look good in English. I tried to imagine how certain pieces would be translated. My conclusion was that it might never be understood in the west. But the modern market has space for all sorts of unusual things. If you're tired of American fantasy, urban fantasy or casual novels - this book is for you.<br />You will love the atmosphere of the World described. Its lore is so grand and detailed - it can easily be compared to that of The Elder Scrolls, Forgotten Realms or other. Although it's not a high fantasy series - there's place for wit and magic.<br />The main character Max (29) is a classical Russian loser of the 90s, who lost all purpose of living in our world, except for the dreams of wonderful places, which he sees. And once he gets a chance to start it over in another reality. And not unlike Harry Potter he discovers himself a prodigy in the World, where he's moved (but also amusingly helpless when it comes to social life and basic survival skills at his new place of living). The character has a very interesting personality and a strange sense of humor, which will likely appeal to the reader. (Hopefully, it won't be lost due to cultural differences)<br />A series of detective stories full of action will follow, involving magic, romance and cozy philosophical chatter. <br /><br />It's a great present for those readers who're ready for something new.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3889704710532561143" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_464730181" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/464730181" />
    <a title="Scott Fabel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8715935-scott-fabel"><img alt="Scott Fabel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1334142766p2/8715935.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/464730181?book_show_action=true">Nov 27, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Scott Fabel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Scott Fabel" href="/user/show/8715935-scott-fabel">Scott Fabel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer464730181" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5135924359044443303">This book, which was originally published in Russia in 1996, introduces the main character (and pseudonymous author) to a completely new world called the Unified Kingdom. After being a complete loser on Earth, Max finds himself as the Nocturnal Representative of the Most Venerable Head of the Minor Secret Investigative Force of the city of Echo. Essentially, he investigates magical mysteries and crimes in this new world. As it turns out, he's quite good at his new job--not a loser at all.<br/><br/>Each ch</span>
  <span id="freeText5135924359044443303" style="display:none">This book, which was originally published in Russia in 1996, introduces the main character (and pseudonymous author) to a completely new world called the Unified Kingdom. After being a complete loser on Earth, Max finds himself as the Nocturnal Representative of the Most Venerable Head of the Minor Secret Investigative Force of the city of Echo. Essentially, he investigates magical mysteries and crimes in this new world. As it turns out, he's quite good at his new job--not a loser at all.<br /><br />Each chapter of the book describes a new adventure that Max must get involved in to solve some kind of mystery or crime. I loved them all. The world described by the author is incredibly creative and playful. Although there are some dark moments in the stories, there is also a lot of humor and quirkiness that makes the story fun to read. The characters are all memorable and interesting in their own right. <br /><br />To be sure, the world and the characters are so well described that I find myself longing to have some kamra (a local beverage) with breakfast, to build at least eight more bathrooms in my house (which is normal in Echo), and to use silent speech (a way of communicating without talking) with all of my friends.<br /><br />If you're looking for a fast-paced and inventive story, I would highly recommend this book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5135924359044443303" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

I read the first book when I was about 12 year old and still no book or books series can out rival Max...The author is amazing, and most of all.. She lives in my country's capital city!!! Omg... <br /><br />So, If you are still just considering reading this book, don't. DO IT. It is complete wonder. But the only problem is, there is only one book translated now, but all books are originally written in Russian, so if you are no stranger to Russian, let yourself into the The Labyrinths of Echo and just hold on, because you WILL be swamp by the story and the characters. :)<br /><br /><br /><br /><br />2016<br />it's even more amazing than the first time</span>
  <a data-text-id="5992895144960733173" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/114711823" />
    <a title="Iain" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/403240-iain"><img alt="Iain" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer11753624354549856980">I wouldn't normally review a book that I haven't finished reading, but I've (at least temporarily) given up on this in favour of other books - and I think that lack of interest is worth a note. Whatever The Stranger tells you it is on the cover, don't believe a word of it. It's not. What it is instead is a strange piece of fantasy where the author is working so hard at creating something original that he's ended up creating something fairly bonkers (and not in a good way). The intricate details </span>
  <span id="freeText11753624354549856980" style="display:none">I wouldn't normally review a book that I haven't finished reading, but I've (at least temporarily) given up on this in favour of other books - and I think that lack of interest is worth a note. Whatever The Stranger tells you it is on the cover, don't believe a word of it. It's not. What it is instead is a strange piece of fantasy where the author is working so hard at creating something original that he's ended up creating something fairly bonkers (and not in a good way). The intricate details and customs of his fantasy world read almost like a pastiche of Victorian fantastic fiction - somewhere in the same vein as Susannah Clarke - only not as interesting, in fact nowhere as interesting. And the translation's annoying too - or maybe that's the original Russian coming out and the translator's being too faithful. Use of language is grating whatever the case.<br /><br />Maybe I'll change my mind if I ever get back to reading it - in which case I'll change the review - but for now I couldn't recommend it. Read The Magicians by Lev Grossman instead - same sort of fiction but much better told.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11753624354549856980" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_48250844" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/48250844" />
    <a title="Shannon (Giraffe Days)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/395599-shannon-giraffe-days"><img alt="Shannon (Giraffe Days)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1420332941p2/395599.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/48250844?book_show_action=true">Mar 04, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shannon (Giraffe Days)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shannon (Giraffe Days)" href="/user/show/395599-shannon-giraffe-days">Shannon (Giraffe Days)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/395599-shannon-giraffe-days?shelf=review-copy">review-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/395599-shannon-giraffe-days?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/395599-shannon-giraffe-days?shelf=2009">2009</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer48250844" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5660541739530634646">Max Frei is a loner in the world, a bit of a chain-smoking bum who's tried fitting in and being normal but doesn't have the heart for it. Only in his dreams is he truly alive. In his dreams, things seem so real that he acts upon them in waking life: if he meets a beautiful new woman in his dreams, he'll break up with his real-life girlfriend. He can quote from books he's read only in his dreams, and visit other places.<br/><br/>One such place he visits regularly is a strange city where the streets are pav</span>
  <span id="freeText5660541739530634646" style="display:none">Max Frei is a loner in the world, a bit of a chain-smoking bum who's tried fitting in and being normal but doesn't have the heart for it. Only in his dreams is he truly alive. In his dreams, things seem so real that he acts upon them in waking life: if he meets a beautiful new woman in his dreams, he'll break up with his real-life girlfriend. He can quote from books he's read only in his dreams, and visit other places.<br /><br />One such place he visits regularly is a strange city where the streets are paved in mosaics and the people wear colourful clothes and turbans. It's here he meets Sir Juffin Hully, who recognises in Max something more than he is in his own world: a magician. Juffin offers Max a job and a home far away from his own, in the city of Echo in the Unified Kingdom.<br /><br />Crossing between worlds is easy enough, and Max loves his new home as he never loved the place where he was born. Concocting a story about his origins to hide the truth, Juffin introduces Max to his colleagues of the Minor Secret Investigative Force at the House by the Bridge and gradually teaches Max some magic, odd bits of history, and how to brew kamra, the stand-in drink for tea and coffee of which the citizens of the Unified Kingdom imbibe in large quantities.<br /><br />Max is launched into this crazy, upbeat world where, if you can't afford to pay for your dinner, the king will happily pick up the tab, and where even dead Grand Magicians cause mayhem. The only thing from his own world that he misses are the cigarettes, but even that small dent in his new-found happiness can be overcome.<br /><br /><br />There are, I believe, ten novels in the series, which have been doing well in Europe for some time now. This is the first time it's been translated into English. Max Frei, aside from being the narrator of the series, is also the pseudonym of Russian novelist Svetlana Martynchik. As part of the zaniness of this novel, it makes perfect sense that Max Frei would be the "author".<br /><br />I'm completely torn as to how to rate this or even to talk about it. There were plenty of times throughout the story when I was confused and a bit annoyed; yet it was also highly original, very fun, quite humorous and definitely quirky - all of which I enjoyed. Let's go over the downside first.<br /><br />From the very beginning, it wasn't an easy book to read. This isn't due to the language but more the style of the prose. What I mean is, the prose isn't difficult to read - it's almost simplistically written - but it's confusing to follow. I think it would be perfectly clear on a second reading, but you'd have to get through a first reading to even reach that stage, so it's not terribly helpful. Part of the problem is that Max doesn't always explain things very well, if at all. I can't figure out who his audience is for this story of his adventurous life, but he vacillates between assuming your prior knowledge to assuming your absolute ignorance. Even when he does try to explain things, I constantly felt that I wasn't on his wavelength and was left feeling more confused, rather than less.<br /><br />Divided into long chapters that each present a different adventure or mystery to be solved, another small thing that bothered me was that I couldn't tell where it was going. There's no over-arching plot, as is typical, which does enhance the "memoir" quality that the author was possibly striving for - but it also leaves me a bit adrift and without much incentive to read on. Never really noticed that before, until it was gone. I happen to find reading about other worlds - like HP - incredibly fun even without an over-arching plot, but it does add excitement and tension and has you gagging for the next book, if done well.<br /><br />There are still some details that I don't understand, like the bit about Max briefly turning into a vampire, and what could possibly be some inconsistencies. But I really want to move on to the positives.<br /><br />The book has been aimed at fans of Sergei Lukyanenko (Night Watch series) and Susanna Clark, but I have to add one of my own: Harry Potter. It's like an adult version of the HP world, with ludicrous titles for things (Order of the Watery Crow, which Max always chuckles at, and his colleague Lonli-Lokli's official title: He Who Snuffs Out Unnecessary Lives, for example) and some crazy, barely edible delicacies. And all the magic, of course, which seems to be made up as it goes along. Which means you never know what this crazy world is going to throw at you next. <br /><br />The tone is light-hearted and silly and nonsensical, which perfectly suits the world and makes it feel more real - but not quite what I was expecting from looking at the cover. The story, the world, its characters, don't take themselves too seriously, Max least of all, and that does lessen any real sense of danger, which would have created a nice balance. <i>The Stranger</i> is what it is and you pretty much just have to go along for the ride and not worry too much - a bit like Max, really. And it is a fascinating world. I just wish it had a bit more darkness to it, and some kind of connecting plotline, to motivate me to read on. At 544 pages it's modestly long for a fantasy novel, but took me a lot longer to read than it should have. It could also do with some tighter proof-reading - always a pet peeve of mine!<br /><br />Overall, it was enjoyable, if perplexing and confusing at times. It'd make a great TV show.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5660541739530634646" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_279631358" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/279631358" />
    <a title="Sharakael" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1746497-sharakael"><img alt="Sharakael" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1227542722p2/1746497.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/279631358?book_show_action=true">Feb 18, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sharakael" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sharakael" href="/user/show/1746497-sharakael">Sharakael</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title=" 9780575089761" href="/book/show/7697125-the-stranger">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746497-sharakael?shelf=unique-fantasy">unique-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746497-sharakael?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746497-sharakael?shelf=detectives">detectives</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer279631358&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer279631358" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4768539810457809415">I feel odd to be giving this book 4*, since normally I'd only give this kind of reading 2*...<br/><br/>Let's see... the main character was, to put it for better or worse, a Marty Stu. He's special with powers and talents which no one else in Echo seemed to have, and blessed with unusually good luck which got him out of sticky situations or delivered the solution to the current problem right into his hands. In other words, he hardly had to work for the achievements he accomplished in this novel. The only t</span>
  <span id="freeText4768539810457809415" style="display:none">I feel odd to be giving this book 4*, since normally I'd only give this kind of reading 2*...<br /><br />Let's see... the main character was, to put it for better or worse, a Marty Stu. He's special with powers and talents which no one else in Echo seemed to have, and blessed with unusually good luck which got him out of sticky situations or delivered the solution to the current problem right into his hands. In other words, he hardly had to work for the achievements he accomplished in this novel. The only thing he failed to get was the girl, so I guess there's some sort of a balance there.<br />Despite how much of a Marty Stu the main character was, he didn't annoy me for some reason... I guess it's probably a wish-fulfilment. Everyone has, at one point or another, dreamed of finding out that s/he's special and not just an everyday joe... and Max Frei sort of provided a fulfilment of that fantasy.<br /><br />The thing which saved this novel for me, I think, are the characters and settings/world. I actually like the supporting characters, and enjoyed reading their conversations. ...I can only mourn the things that would had been lost in translation, as I have a feeling they're more entertaining in the original Russian.<br /><br />And personally, I adore a well-built world/setting, and I found that reading and learning about Echo was enjoyable. I like how the details of the world was revealed bits by bits; the book never did an info/history dump on its readers.<br /><br />I like the structure of the novel too... instead of 1 long story that spanned the whole book, instead you get 'cases', so in that sense this novel is more like a collection of short stories. And maybe that's a reason why reading this novel felt simply like reading the daily life of Max Frei. You don't get the tension of a reading a full-length mystery novel... instead you get smaller doses of mystery which served to introduce the world and its characters, and seeing how they spend their time in between solving mysteries.<br /><br />Overall this was a chance purchase which I didn't anticipate liking... will be ordering the next books in the series soon.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4768539810457809415" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1911890992696549071"><br/> "Max Frei" - ie Svetlana Martynchik - has published this mammoth series Labyrinths of Echo of which The Stranger is the opening - I think it's 10 volumes so far - to great acclaim and success in Russia and Europe from the mid 90's on, so I was very curious about this book. <br/><br/>Overall I was disappointed because the book just did not engage me; it's not bad but I've read too many similar but better books to waste too much time on it. <br/><br/> I could not care less about its main character or the rest of the</span>
  <span id="freeText1911890992696549071" style="display:none"><br /> "Max Frei" - ie Svetlana Martynchik - has published this mammoth series Labyrinths of Echo of which The Stranger is the opening - I think it's 10 volumes so far - to great acclaim and success in Russia and Europe from the mid 90's on, so I was very curious about this book. <br /><br />Overall I was disappointed because the book just did not engage me; it's not bad but I've read too many similar but better books to waste too much time on it. <br /><br /> I could not care less about its main character or the rest of the cast and the weirdness, the "unusual" of the book did not keep my attention for long. <br /><br /> I guess a shorter and more to the point review should just say "not for me", too little time, too many interesting books to waste it on something passable but not more...<br /></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/115899053?book_show_action=true">Aug 08, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elvira Atvara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elvira Atvara" href="/user/show/3153070-elvira-atvara">Elvira Atvara</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer115899053" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer7402753490961098050">Take Terry Prattchet and mix his Discworld with a bit of Harry Potter's adventures and you will get the general idea of the awesomeness of this book. It is ironic and funny, but not to the extent of Discworld, where there is more ironical discourse than action. <br/><br/>There is only one little criticism... Frei should never be read when hungry or full, because no matter what, it makes you crave food with its mouthwashing descriptions of Chakata pie and other magical foods. The best condition for this bo</span>
  <span id="freeText7402753490961098050" style="display:none">Take Terry Prattchet and mix his Discworld with a bit of Harry Potter's adventures and you will get the general idea of the awesomeness of this book. It is ironic and funny, but not to the extent of Discworld, where there is more ironical discourse than action. <br /><br />There is only one little criticism... Frei should never be read when hungry or full, because no matter what, it makes you crave food with its mouthwashing descriptions of Chakata pie and other magical foods. The best condition for this book is to read it at the dinner table - even the most simple sandwich will taste like heaven with a bit of help of Frei's magical words.<br /></span>

<div id="review_873035489" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/873035489" />
    <a title="Karla Huebner" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4588864-karla-huebner"><img alt="Karla Huebner" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1327888200p2/4588864.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/873035489?book_show_action=true">Mar 05, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Karla Huebner" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Karla Huebner" href="/user/show/4588864-karla-huebner">Karla Huebner</a>
      </span>

          added it


          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781590203316" href="/book/show/7651682-the-stranger">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4588864-karla-huebner?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4588864-karla-huebner?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4588864-karla-huebner?shelf=russian">russian</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer873035489" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2232211961318125313">Review of this book are sharply divided between those who adore it and those who were deeply disappointed and felt it didn't live up to its billing as brilliant, hilarious, satirical, and philosophical. A third category of reviews deals with the problem of translation: some readers loved it in Russian but think the English translation is a flop, or that perhaps the book can't quite be translated. While I don't read Russian, I think my reaction has to fall into the third category.<br/>First off: no, I</span>
  <span id="freeText2232211961318125313" style="display:none">Review of this book are sharply divided between those who adore it and those who were deeply disappointed and felt it didn't live up to its billing as brilliant, hilarious, satirical, and philosophical. A third category of reviews deals with the problem of translation: some readers loved it in Russian but think the English translation is a flop, or that perhaps the book can't quite be translated. While I don't read Russian, I think my reaction has to fall into the third category.<br />First off: no, I did not think comparisons with Harry Potter or Susanna Clarke were beneficial. Such comparisons to other books/authors usually annoy me anyway, because they imply more similarity than is likely to exist. I like both the Harry Potter books and Clarke's <i>Jonathan Strange and Mr. Norrell,</i> but the main thing this has in common with them is that it's about magic. The Harry Potter books are children's literature that adults also enjoy, with struggles between good and evil and lots of cliff-hanging adventure. <i>Strange</i> is an intricate, very literate, highly sophisticated novel. And what exactly is <i>The Stranger</i>? Well, that's the question.<br />The book is unquestionably fantasy; it's about a pleasant guy named Max who never did very well at anything because he's fundamentally nocturnal. Max visits another world in his dreams, and is recruited there to stay and join a squad of sort of magic detectives (in contrast to the mostly bumbling and oafish regular police). The premise is good and the author (who is female and apparently collaborates to some extent with her husband) is extremely inventive. As one reads, it becomes clear that there isn't really a plot; it's a set of linked cases, with the final one giving the impression for awhile that something dire will happen to the narrator, but even though people occasionally do die in the book (murders get investigated), everything remains rather like a souffle or a cream-puff. And, given the emphasis on food in the book, I think that's a fair comparison in more ways than one.<br />The book was quirky and imaginative enough that I gradually made my way through the whole thing. Yet I kept feeling that either this book was massively over-hyped or it really lost a lot in translation. Sure, it's kind of funny, but in English I'd say it's only mildly funny. It feels like it ought to be much funnier. Philosophical? Well, more so than the average best-seller, but the philosophical aspect only surfaces now and then, and not very noticeably because the philosophical bits are obscured by verbiage and flights of fancy. Satirical? I wasn't sure what it was supposed to be satirizing, as while it makes reference to earlier fantasies and detective fiction, I didn't feel it was satirizing them, but rather playfully riffing on some of their conventions.<br />At times I liked the book quite a bit and felt I should avoid judging it by standards that perhaps shouldn't apply to it. At other times I was reminded of reading <i>The Master and Margarita</i> and wondering whether stylistic flourishes that work in Russian just sound clunky in English--after all, I've found that paragraphs by Jaroslav Seifert that read perfectly nicely in Czech struck me as more limping than limpid when I translated them.<br />For awhile I kept thinking that the dialog in the book is too undifferentiated as far as voice; it all felt the same to me, in a bad way. But first it occurred to me that plenty of wonderful English fiction has characters whose diction doesn't vary much, and next I realized that the dialog in this book actually varies more than it seems to. So that suggests translation problems. The book certainly seems rather verbose, which I'm confident is partly a translation problem as English often requires more words to get across an idea that a Slavic language can convey with economy.<br />Ultimately, I don't think English readers can be getting anything like what Russian readers are enjoying. There's also the problem of cultural differences, and of course that not everyone will like fairly plotless wild fantasies in which very little is ever explained.<br />Still, the thing has enough pull to it that I've begun the second of the numerous books in the series. I probably won't read beyond the second, but as I got the two volumes free at a Slavic conference, and enjoy the vivid imagination, I may as well see what happens next.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2232211961318125313" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_912976271" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/912976271" />
    <a title="Elizabeth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17203750-elizabeth"><img alt="Elizabeth" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/912976271?book_show_action=true">Apr 17, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elizabeth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elizabeth" href="/user/show/17203750-elizabeth">Elizabeth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer912976271" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17918251033809613344">For all of the English speaking readers out there I would like to point out that the translation of this amazing book has gone beyond salvagable. Not only do parts of text seem to be missing but also other parts of text seemingly appear out of nowhere(!). Some jokes have gotten simply scrapped, literally scrapped, and at parts the characters react differently from in the book. e.g.: somebody scowling at a joke instead of laughing out loud [page 107(E), 126(R)]. This is only one example among hun</span>
  <span id="freeText17918251033809613344" style="display:none">For all of the English speaking readers out there I would like to point out that the translation of this amazing book has gone beyond salvagable. Not only do parts of text seem to be missing but also other parts of text seemingly appear out of nowhere(!). Some jokes have gotten simply scrapped, literally scrapped, and at parts the characters react differently from in the book. e.g.: somebody scowling at a joke instead of laughing out loud [page 107(E), 126(R)]. This is only one example among hundreds.<br />I can only imagine that the translators at some point went and said: 'Yeah, well you know, the English readers won't understand Max at all, so instead we will make his world a much darker place and leave out a lot of good humor and natural joie de vivre that was this book's major turn on. Why did they do this? I do not know, I simply canot believe that native English speakers are so much different from Russian readers that they had to adapt the book for them. At points I really wanted to cry seeing how they had mangled and torn at my favorite book.<br />One more thing. In the Russian edition there is an intro that fairly well explains how Max got mixed up in all of this and which sets the mood for the entire series. In the English translation it was simply scrapped. That is all. I do not have anything more to add besides how sorry I am for the people who will probably never get to read a decent rendition of this masterpiece. I am afraid the damage is done, and because of it's low success they won't retranslate it again. This makes me sad.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17918251033809613344" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer213300569" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer6644530540598251298">What a complete waste of time. The idea that this is only the first in a series of volumes makes me contemplate dramatic self-injury. Seriously, given the choice of not being able to read for pleasure for a decade or reading the next installment of Frei's saga, I'd go philistine in a minute. <br/><br/>The premise of this book was so promising - indeed, I discovered it in the Russian section of Idlewild Books in Manhattan this summer, and later ordered a used copy on amazon. Looking back on the back cover </span>
  <span id="freeText6644530540598251298" style="display:none">What a complete waste of time. The idea that this is only the first in a series of volumes makes me contemplate dramatic self-injury. Seriously, given the choice of not being able to read for pleasure for a decade or reading the next installment of Frei's saga, I'd go philistine in a minute. <br /><br />The premise of this book was so promising - indeed, I discovered it in the Russian section of Idlewild Books in Manhattan this summer, and later ordered a used copy on amazon. Looking back on the back cover pitch, I see now that the description was technically accurate, but not in any way I would have imagined. For the worse. <br /><br />What makes me have such disdain for this book? Well, the dialogue, primarily. It singlehandedly ruins the potentially wonderful oddball bits. Instead, it is grandiose, mannerly, and pointless. And, worst of all, neverending. This book contains a handful of vignettes, but somehow stretches them to the point of several hundred pages. If you think that sounds like a lot of nonsense, you are right on the money.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1179958221" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1179958221" />
    <a title="Tim Hicks" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/111076-tim-hicks"><img alt="Tim Hicks" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1327258501p2/111076.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1179958221?book_show_action=true">Jan 25, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tim Hicks" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tim Hicks" href="/user/show/111076-tim-hicks">Tim Hicks</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/111076-tim-hicks?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1179958221" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11060673979493383085">I don't speak Russian so I will have to judge the English version on its own merits. <br/>I liked it a lot. <br/><br/>Others have compared it to Harry Potter but I think that's off the mark. More like a combination of Jack Vance and Steven Brust. <br/> <br/>Some have said it's a series of pointless episodes; I disagree. I kept catching little hints about what's really going on here and how it relates to our hero's home world. I may be wrong here, because if there really are ten volumes in this series it shouldn't take t</span>
  <span id="freeText11060673979493383085" style="display:none">I don't speak Russian so I will have to judge the English version on its own merits. <br />I liked it a lot. <br /><br />Others have compared it to Harry Potter but I think that's off the mark. More like a combination of Jack Vance and Steven Brust. <br /> <br />Some have said it's a series of pointless episodes; I disagree. I kept catching little hints about what's really going on here and how it relates to our hero's home world. I may be wrong here, because if there really are ten volumes in this series it shouldn't take that long to reveal the framework. And why the world/country is called Echo. There's even a hint that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[our hero may have actually died in his home world <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, in which case there may not be much more to reveal. <br /> <br />Also, if I read many more in the series, I may throw the book across the room after the 30th mention of kamra. In this one, I actually went back and counted. From its first mention on page 11 to the end of page 110 - a hundred pages - we have at least 32 mentions of kamra. <br /> <br />But there is creativity here, and plenty of it. Memory birds. Magic at many levels, with bureaucratic restrictions on some of it and practical restrictions on other parts. A lot of delightfully nutty people. <br /><br />Also wondered how Max managed an amorous evening with Melamori without ever letting go of the bad guy he had captured by miniaturization. I'm prepared to allow almost anything in fantasy, but we do have to be careful with the details. <br /><br />I will look for #2, at least. </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/34443065?book_show_action=true">Oct 03, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="J.A." class="user" itemprop="url" name="J.A." href="/user/show/1049480-j-a">J.A.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1049480-j-a?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1049480-j-a?shelf=did-not-finish">did-not-finish</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1049480-j-a?shelf=%D1%80%D1%83%D1%81%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%8F-%D0%BB%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%82%D1%83%D1%80%D0%B0">русская-литература</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer34443065" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7679254103720584270">Where do you shelve a book that you won't finish reading? It would be disingenuous to place it on the read shelf, and yet it does not belong on the to-read shelf since I have no intention of returning to it. Is the only other option to delete it altogether? My solution was to create a new did-not-finish shelf. I wouldn't say this book is so dreadful it deserves the ignominy of being the sole occupant of this undesirable shelf, but I don't want to accumulate books on this shelf, either.<br/><br/>This book </span>
  <span id="freeText7679254103720584270" style="display:none">Where do you shelve a book that you won't finish reading? It would be disingenuous to place it on the read shelf, and yet it does not belong on the to-read shelf since I have no intention of returning to it. Is the only other option to delete it altogether? My solution was to create a new did-not-finish shelf. I wouldn't say this book is so dreadful it deserves the ignominy of being the sole occupant of this undesirable shelf, but I don't want to accumulate books on this shelf, either.<br /><br />This book has been a sensation in Russia, so naturally I was curious about it. After reading half of it the only sensation I felt was drowsiness, and its popularity is a curiosity indeed. Sleep is a recurring theme in the book, as Max dreams his initial contact with Sir Juffin Hully, who then transports him to the magical realm of Echo, where he is frequently assailed in his nightmares. Max's narration had a magical somnolent effect on me, and reading this book felt like one of those nightmares wherein you attempt to run but cannot move your feet.<br /><br />As other reviewers have pointed out, this edition suffers from a poor translation. The language is colloquial and cliche, preventing the English reader from appreciating the whimsical story. I could try to read it in the original Russian, but I'd rather spend my time on other promising books instead.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7679254103720584270" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4277139278714348412">Rereading this book was a great experience. This is an unusual book. I understand this now more than when I was reading it back in 2007, I've read more books now and this one still stands out.<br/><br/>The great thing about this book is that it submerges you in an emotional state of comfortable uncertainty – you don't know what to expect but you know it's going to be pleasant and magical.<br/><br/>I tried preparing for a tabletop role-playing game in the universe of this book, but it seems incredibly difficult, the</span>
  <span id="freeText4277139278714348412" style="display:none">Rereading this book was a great experience. This is an unusual book. I understand this now more than when I was reading it back in 2007, I've read more books now and this one still stands out.<br /><br />The great thing about this book is that it submerges you in an emotional state of comfortable uncertainty – you don't know what to expect but you know it's going to be pleasant and magical.<br /><br />I tried preparing for a tabletop role-playing game in the universe of this book, but it seems incredibly difficult, the magic barely has an underlying principle that could help measure and limit the powers available to inhabitants of this world, professions aren't extremely well-defined, and very few people are having grand adventures in this world that could be compared to the ones the main character goes on. This world is tailored for him and his growing limitless set of incredible (by this world's) powers. The main character is lucky and blissful, successful in most things he tries and is a joy to watch, many powerful mages of this book world are enjoying his adventures and so does the reader. However, living in this world isn't as interesting if you're not in that circle of powerful mages.</span>

<div id="review_1680204276" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1680204276" />
    <a title="Molly Mix" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/677912-molly-mix"><img alt="Molly Mix" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1360620728p2/677912.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1680204276" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7997965361607575229">The hero of this book was advertised as a grown up Harry Potter, if Harry Potter drank and smoke cigarettes and swore. Since I haven't read Harry Potter yet (I know, I know!), that didn't mean a whole heck of a lot to me. I mean, I know a little. And I have seen the first few movies. Regardless, I was intrigued. It took a while to get into, I'll admit - it took me nearly year to finish the first quarter of the book, reading just a few pages at a time. Once it hit its stride, it took just a week </span>
  <span id="freeText7997965361607575229" style="display:none">The hero of this book was advertised as a grown up Harry Potter, if Harry Potter drank and smoke cigarettes and swore. Since I haven't read Harry Potter yet (I know, I know!), that didn't mean a whole heck of a lot to me. I mean, I know a little. And I have seen the first few movies. Regardless, I was intrigued. It took a while to get into, I'll admit - it took me nearly year to finish the first quarter of the book, reading just a few pages at a time. Once it hit its stride, it took just a week or two to finish the rest. I think one of the reasons it took me so long to get into it, was that the world Mr. Frei was building was so radically different, it took me awhile to start to think of it as a familiar enough place to want to go back to. Once it did though, I was able to appreciate just how novel and unique the world was. And the characters. And the magic. And the story. It genuinely was magical.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7997965361607575229" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3060685243" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6959680369375831353">It's my guilty pleasure book. World is beautiful, magical and vibrant, really one where you would be happy to lost yourself in, characters are funny and likable. Short stories which this book consists of are interesting and entertaining. <br/><br/>But at the same time, I'm getting tired of "chosen one" thingy. Main character has too much power (even though he barely controls it) and get everything way too easy which stops a character development. I just truly wish they would make it a little more deep in </span>
  <span id="freeText6959680369375831353" style="display:none">It's my guilty pleasure book. World is beautiful, magical and vibrant, really one where you would be happy to lost yourself in, characters are funny and likable. Short stories which this book consists of are interesting and entertaining. <br /><br />But at the same time, I'm getting tired of "chosen one" thingy. Main character has too much power (even though he barely controls it) and get everything way too easy which stops a character development. I just truly wish they would make it a little more deep in this regard.<br /><br />Still, I'm ready to forgive a lot for this beautifully written world which makes me value more simple pleasures like a walk in a beautiful city, nice food, cozy cafes and a company of good friends. <br /><br />Can I recommend it? It touches me but there are a lot of weak points as well. Try it, maybe you will lose yourself too in these tight, cozy, mosaic streets of Echo city. </span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/114444125-teodora?shelf=well-developed-worlds">well-developed-worlds</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3568607320" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9271789537830449784">Escapism at its finest.<br/>If you’re looking for a complex plot full of action and conflicts, this is not the book for you. I can only describe this book as cosy, a read that you really look forward to come back to after a day of hard work and worries IRL to be swept away into the fascinating and welcoming world of Echo.<br/>Max is a young man in his twenties suffering from mild depression who cannot find a suitable place for himself in our world on Earth and has troubles accepting the mundane routine of</span>
  <span id="freeText9271789537830449784" style="display:none">Escapism at its finest.<br />If you’re looking for a complex plot full of action and conflicts, this is not the book for you. I can only describe this book as cosy, a read that you really look forward to come back to after a day of hard work and worries IRL to be swept away into the fascinating and welcoming world of Echo.<br />Max is a young man in his twenties suffering from mild depression who cannot find a suitable place for himself in our world on Earth and has troubles accepting the mundane routine of our everyday reality. His only escape is dreaming - something he’s only able to do during the day - and in his dreams he gets a job offer that turns out to be a magical door to the life he’s always yearned for.<br />I haven’t read the Russian version of The Stranger and, while the translation is very good, I do appreciate that some of the humour does get lost. Still, though, if you enjoy rich world-building and a pleasant journey through calm waters into the sunset, definitely give this book a go.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('4fFEDKFJNy6VOW4uLtGfHbIq5L7lUnPEXHrR4GXHQ8smJ50q7kqWTIu8Q/qVZkE4S0Q2wKonPme9EohKh6FOeA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  </b>
</p><p>"Max Frei" is a pen-name of Svetlana Martynchik. She has created the well-known Echo series. Svetlana Yuryevna Martynchik is a Russian writer and artist.</p><p>Martynchik studied at the philological department of Odessa State University, but dropped out without graduating. Martynchik lived in Moscow since 1993 and lives in Vilnius since 2004.</p><p>For more details see <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Svetlana_Martynchik' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Wikipedia: <i>Svetlana M</i></a></p></span>
